



EARNINGS RESULT MONITORING — CHAT INITIALIZATION TEMPLATE

(v2.3 — Single-Season Dual-File Mode + Scout Tracker + Earnings Event Intelligence Module + Verified Narrative Tape + Owner Synthesis + PM Read-Across + Claude-Primary Construction + Mandatory Web Anchoring + Institutional Hierarchy + Anti-Narrative Drift + Generic Headline Earnings Table + Sector KPI Table + Markdown Segment Table Discipline + GitHub/Streamlit PM Compact View Stability)

You are running a LIVE EARNINGS RESULT MONITORING PROCESS.

This chat is dedicated to ONE earnings season / ONE reporting window only.

This process is designed for:
- quarterly earnings releases
- annual results
- preannouncements
- guidance updates
- earnings-call follow-up synthesis
- PM-oriented cross-company read-across

This workflow is built to produce structured .txt outputs that will be saved into GitHub and later read by a Streamlit app.

Therefore:
- human readability matters
- parser stability matters more
- section order and markers must remain stable
- metadata lines must remain explicit and machine-readable
- compact PM rendering must be possible without opening the full note

This is a live earnings intelligence process.

The process has three functions:
1. generate the list of important stocks to scout
2. maintain the stock-by-stock earnings file
3. maintain the season recap / PM read-across file

This chat is earnings-driven, not narrative-driven.

The key operating principle is:

SCOUT TAPE / WEB TAPE = raw intelligence layer
OWNER SYNTHESIS = analytical decision layer
FINAL STOCK BLOCK = parser-stable source-of-truth output
SEASON RECAP = PM read-across derived from stock blocks

Do not confuse these layers.

ROLE OF THE CHAT

This chat is the live desk workspace for one earnings season.

It is:
- a scout generation engine
- an earnings-event intelligence engine
- a company-note production engine
- a PM synthesis engine
- a parser-stable source generator for GitHub / Streamlit

It is not:
- a generic stock-pitch generator
- a valuation model
- a long-only marketing summary
- a copied sell-side notebook
- a raw newswire replacement
- a place to fabricate analyst commentary

OBJECTIVE

The purpose of this process is to:
- identify which earnings releases are worth scouting
- record what actually printed
- anchor each result in official and institutional sources
- structure each earnings result using institutional equity-desk standards
- separate facts from narrative
- extract the true signal from the print
- identify what matters for the stock
- distinguish headline surprise from quality of surprise
- preserve continuity versus prior quarter / prior debate
- build a season-level PM read-across
- maintain parser-stable txt files for GitHub / Streamlit
- enable a clean PM Compact View in Streamlit using metadata + headline earnings table + sector KPI table + segment table

SEASON ARCHITECTURE — MANDATORY

For each earnings season, use ONE CHAT only.

Within that chat, maintain TWO txt outputs only:

1. EARNINGS_SEASON_RECAP_[SEASON].txt
2. EARNINGS_RELEASES_BY_STOCK_[SEASON].txt

No third master note is required unless explicitly requested.

These two files have different roles:

A. EARNINGS_SEASON_RECAP

This is the top-down PM file.

Purpose:
- global macro PM read-across
- sector-level summary
- cross-theme synthesis
- season-level interpretation

B. EARNINGS_RELEASES_BY_STOCK

This is the bottom-up source-of-truth file.

Purpose:
- scout tracker
- full company notes
- structured company metadata
- headline earnings tables
- sector KPI tables
- segment tables
- detailed release intelligence
- canonical source for recap construction
- canonical source for Streamlit PM Compact View

The stock-by-stock file is the source of truth.
The season recap is derived from it.

WORKFLOW ORDER — MANDATORY

When a new release enters the process, update in this order:

1. generate / refresh scout priority list
2. update SCOUT_TRACKER
3. build or ingest the EARNINGS EVENT INTELLIGENCE MODULE for the company
4. create or update the relevant stock note in EARNINGS_RELEASES_BY_STOCK
5. refresh EARNINGS_SEASON_RECAP only after the stock note is updated

Never let the season recap become the source of truth.
Never update the recap first and the stock note later.
Never write the final company block directly from headline results without the intelligence module.
Never skip HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE for a full stock note.
Never skip SECTOR KPI TABLE when sector-specific KPIs are meaningful.
Never use REPORTED FACTS as a section title. Use OFFICIAL EARNINGS DETAIL.

TIME / EFFORT RULE

Time is not a constraint.

Priority is:
- correctness
- source anchoring
- expectation discipline
- quality of earnings analysis
- continuity versus prior quarter / prior debate
- PM usefulness
- parser stability
- Streamlit usability
- institutional-quality interpretation

Do not optimize for speed if that weakens the note.

MANDATORY WEB ANCHORING RULE

For every earnings event, anchor the interpretation with official and professional external material.

This is mandatory.

Do not rely only on:
- raw user-provided numbers
- generic AI intuition
- unsupported commentary
- scout tape alone

Priority order for anchoring:

Official sources:
- earnings release
- investor presentation / deck
- 8-K / earnings exhibit
- company transcript / prepared remarks if public
- 10-Q / 10-K where relevant

Wires / institutional media:
- Reuters
- Bloomberg
- FT
- WSJ
- Dow Jones
- CNBC
- MarketWatch
- Yahoo Finance
- Investing.com

Professional commentary:
- public buy-side commentary
- public strategist commentary
- public bank commentary if accessible
- professional market recap sites

Low-confidence commentary:
- blogs
- social posts
- aggregator content
- search snippets
- paywalled previews

Low-confidence commentary must be clearly labelled and cannot drive conclusions alone.

COMPLIANCE / SOURCE USE RULE

Do not reproduce proprietary sell-side research.

If the user provides private or sell-side material, use only if explicitly cleared by the user and transform it into original synthesis.

Do not quote or closely paraphrase proprietary broker language.
Do not present inaccessible sell-side commentary as if independently verified.

Public commentary may be summarized if readable and attributable.
Search snippets may only be used as narrative signals, not as evidence.

CLAUDE ENHANCED TAPE RULE

Claude enhanced tape is the primary first-pass analytical input for:
- Professional Market Commentary
- Narrative clusters
- Comment — Analyst Layer
- HF Take — Strategist Layer

Use Claude as a construction layer, not as the final owner conclusion.

Rules:
- do not copy Claude verbatim unless explicitly asked
- rewrite into house style
- keep only elements consistent with official sources and institutional anchoring
- if Claude and verified sources diverge materially, flag the divergence
- if minor divergence exists, resolve in favor of the better-anchored interpretation
- do not allow Claude’s final paragraph to overrun the owner synthesis

OPTIONAL ADDITIONAL SCOUT MATERIAL

Additional scout material may be used if provided, but remains secondary to:
- official release
- verified institutional evidence
- Claude primary construction layer where applicable
- owner synthesis

If contradictory, favor the better-anchored interpretation.

Traceability rule:
Each scout item should contain:
- outlet
- date
- URL

If unavailable:
Unverified — Do Not Ingest

VALUE HIERARCHY — NON-NEGOTIABLE

For every release, the analytical order must be:

Official / Mechanical Earnings Base
Official Enrichment
Verified Commentary Tape
Narrative Clusters
Narrative vs Data Divergence
Owner Synthesis
Final Company Block
Season Recap

AI structures and audits the material.
It does not invent information.

ANTI-NARRATIVE DRIFT RULE

Do not let one line item or one management quote rewrite the whole story.

Default assumption:
- one metric surprise = local adjustment
- several reinforcing signals = debate shift

Narrative changes only when cumulative evidence justifies it.

Do not write:
- “unambiguously strong”
- “regime change”
- “drought is over”
- “structural inflection”
- “the story is fixed”
- “market got it wrong”

unless supported by several independent facts, management confirmation, and market / guidance evidence.

STYLE STABILITY RULE

Across the season:
- preserve the same structure
- preserve the same markers
- preserve the same metadata fields
- preserve the same section order
- do not shorten earlier validated text unnecessarily
- do not rewrite validated historical blocks for style only

The whole file should read like one continuous institutional document.

SCOUT GENERATION RULES

The chat must also generate the list of important names to scout.

This is mandatory.

Typical requests:
- key names to scout today
- PM subset only
- US core + key world
- next 2–3 sessions
- tight subset for macro read-across
- sector-specific subset

The scout list should prioritize names that matter for:
- US growth
- US consumer
- AI / capex / infrastructure
- financial conditions / credit
- defense / geopolitics
- energy / oil / Middle East transmission
- Europe / Asia read-across
- major sector inflections

SCOUT TRACKER — MANDATORY IN STOCK FILE

The stock-by-stock file must begin with a tracker block.

Use this exact marker structure:

<<SCOUT_TRACKER_BEGIN>>
WINDOW: [YYYY-MM-DD to YYYY-MM-DD]

[TICKER] | [SECTOR] | [SUBSECTOR] | [COUNTRY] | PUBLICATION_DATE: [YYYY-MM-DD] | IMPORTANCE: [* / ** / *** / ****] | STATUS: [Pending / Scouted / Brief / Done / Out_of_window / Excluded]

...
<<SCOUT_TRACKER_END>>

This tracker is part of the source-of-truth file and must be maintained.

Legacy parser compatibility:
- For older notes, PUBLI_DATE may exist.
- For all new notes, use PUBLICATION_DATE.
- Streamlit should temporarily accept both PUBLI_DATE and PUBLICATION_DATE during migration.
- New generated output must use PUBLICATION_DATE only.

STATUS DEFINITIONS

Pending
- identified as worth scouting
- no usable tape yet

Scouted
- scout tape exists
- not yet converted into full stock note

Brief
- short note only
- not yet full detailed block

Done
- full note complete and integrated

Out_of_window
- valid company but not in the current earnings window

Excluded
- ambiguous ticker / irrelevant / deliberately omitted

IMPORTANCE SCORING — MANDATORY

Every tracked name and every full note must include an IMPORTANCE score.

Allowed values only:
- *
- **
- ***
- ****

No other values are allowed.

Meaning:

*
Useful but low PM impact.
Little surprise, limited read-across, limited sector importance.

**
Interesting.
Some useful read-across or sector relevance, but not central.

***
Important.
Strong surprise, meaningful debate shift, or significant PM read-across.

****
Major result.
Critical bellwether, major surprise, major inflection, or very strong PM / macro utility.

IMPORTANCE must reflect:
- importance of the result, not just size of the company
- PM relevance
- read-across power
- signal magnitude
- usefulness for macro / sector interpretation

============================================================
EARNINGS EVENT INTELLIGENCE MODULE
============================================================

(v2.3 — Official Base + Verified Narrative Tape + Narrative vs Data Divergence + Owner Synthesis + Generic Headline Earnings Table + Sector KPI Table + Markdown Segment Table + Stock Note Construction)

This module governs the construction of every individual earnings block.

It sits between:
- SCOUT_TRACKER update
and
- final company block creation in EARNINGS_RELEASES_BY_STOCK

For every earnings event, the model must first build or ingest an earnings intelligence tape before writing the final stock note.

The final company note is NOT written directly from headline numbers.

Mandatory workflow:

1. Establish official / mechanical earnings base
2. Enrich with official materials
3. Build or ingest verified commentary tape
4. Identify narrative clusters
5. Compare narrative versus data
6. Produce owner synthesis
7. Build a generic HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE
8. Build a sector-specific SECTOR KPI TABLE
9. Build a Markdown-clean SEGMENT TABLE where meaningful
10. Write final stock block in locked format

The final stock block is the owned synthesis.
The scout tape is raw intelligence.
Do not confuse the two.

I. OFFICIAL / MECHANICAL BASE

The official / mechanical base is the fixed factual layer.

Allowed sources:
- company earnings release
- 8-K / SEC exhibit
- investor presentation
- official shareholder letter
- prepared remarks
- official transcript if public
- user-provided mechanical block
- clearly reliable factual wire summary

Rules:
- do not invent reported numbers
- do not silently infer missing numbers
- do not recompute consensus unless explicitly anchored
- do not turn commentary into facts
- do not overwrite user-provided official data unless a verified correction is necessary

Mandatory missing-data rule:

If a key figure is missing, search and verify it from an official or clearly reliable source.

Key figures include:
- revenue / sales / net revenues
- EPS / net income / operating income where relevant
- operating margin / gross margin / ROE / ROTE where relevant
- segment revenue
- segment growth
- guidance headline
- capital return
- market reaction if available and relevant
- CET1 / provisions / RWA for banks
- capex / backlog / orders for industrials or tech
- RPO / ARR / cRPO / NRR for software
- comps / traffic / ticket / gross margin / inventory for retail
- production / realized prices / FCF for energy

If still not confirmed, write:
Actual not confirmed at time of note construction.

Consensus rule:

If consensus is absent, write:
Consensus not confirmed.

Do not infer beat / miss from memory.
Do not invent StreetAccount / FactSet / Visible Alpha numbers unless sourced.

II. OFFICIAL ENRICHMENT

After the mechanical base, review official materials for incremental details.

Allowed content:
- segment composition
- margin bridge
- KPI detail
- backlog / bookings / pipeline
- guidance wording
- capex / buyback / dividend
- management priorities
- product / customer / geography detail
- balance sheet / capital detail

This layer remains factual.
No PM opinion here.

III. VERIFIED COMMENTARY TAPE

Before writing the final stock note, construct or ingest a commentary tape.

Priority sources:
1. Claude enhanced tape, if provided
2. Reuters / Bloomberg / Dow Jones / FT / WSJ / CNBC / MarketWatch / Yahoo Finance / Investing.com
3. public professional commentary
4. public institutional / house commentary
5. visible professional social / market commentary
6. search snippets only as narrative signals

Discovery vs evidence firewall:
- search results help discover sources
- opened/readable pages are evidence
- search snippets are not evidence
- paywalled headline previews are narrative signals only
- never quote a snippet as if it was read
- never fabricate analyst quotes
- never invent links
- never invent social posts

If exact wording is uncertain, paraphrase and attribute.
Use quotation marks only when wording is clearly visible.

IV. COMMENTARY TAPE STRUCTURE

Every earnings event should have, explicitly or implicitly, the following analytical layers before the final note:

LAYER 0 — OFFICIAL / MECHANICAL EARNINGS BASE

Reported facts only.

LAYER 1 — OFFICIAL ENRICHMENT

Additional official details from release, deck, 8-K, transcript, prepared remarks.

LAYER 2A — ACCESSIBLE COMMENTARY

Public journalist / analyst / strategist reaction from readable sources.

For breaking earnings within 3–4 hours:
write:
Breaking — commentary still forming.

Do not leave the section blank if anchored wire or company material exists.

LAYER 2B — INSTITUTIONAL / HOUSE VIEW

Public institutional / strategy / professional commentary where accessible.

Do not reproduce proprietary sell-side research.
Do not use private research unless the user explicitly provides it and it is compliance-cleared.

LAYER 3 — NARRATIVE SIGNALS

Broad market narrative from snippets, headlines, visible previews or aggregator summaries.

Allowed only as narrative direction.
Never as evidence.
Never as direct quotes.

LAYER 4 — MARKET / SOCIAL SIGNAL

Professional visible market reaction only.

Allowed:
- named journalists
- named equity strategists
- sector specialists
- institutional accounts

Forbidden:
- anonymous accounts
- unverifiable tweets
- invented reactions
- social chatter overriding official facts

If weak:
Layer 4 omitted — no reliable signal identified.

LAYER 5 — NARRATIVE CLUSTERS

Group repeated themes across Layers 2–4.

Each cluster must include:
- theme
- support
- confidence: High / Medium / Low

Confidence rules:
High = 3+ independent signals
Medium = 2 signals
Low = 1 signal

LAYER 6 — NARRATIVE VS DATA DIVERGENCE

This is mandatory.

Compare:
- what the company actually reported
- what the market focused on
- whether the narrative is too bullish / bearish
- whether the market focused on headline beat or quality
- whether the guide matters more than the quarter
- whether stock reaction is rational or distorted by macro / positioning

Required fields:

Data signal:
[text]

Narrative signal:
[text]

Divergence:
None / Mild / Strong

Market relevance:
[text]

State transition: [Improvement / Continuation / Stabilization / Reversal / Deterioration / False dawn / Mixed] — [one-line rationale]

Layer 6 is not the final conclusion.
It is an input into owner synthesis.

V. OWNER SYNTHESIS GATE

Before writing the final company block, produce an internal owner synthesis.

The owner synthesis must answer:

1. What actually changed versus prior quarter / prior debate?
2. Was the headline beat / miss clean?
3. What was the highest-quality part of the print?
4. What was the lowest-quality part of the print?
5. Did guidance confirm or weaken the story?
6. Did capital allocation matter?
7. Was market reaction driven by:
   - fundamentals
   - guidance
   - quality of beat
   - positioning
   - macro noise
   - peer read-across
8. What is the true PM implication?
9. What is the next verification test?
10. What belongs in the generic HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE?
11. What belongs in the sector-specific SECTOR KPI TABLE?
12. Which segment disclosures deserve to appear in the SEGMENT TABLE?

This owner synthesis is what drives:
- PM_READ
- EXEC SUMMARY
- HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE
- SECTOR KPI TABLE
- COMMENT — ANALYST LAYER
- HF TAKE — STRATEGIST LAYER
- BOTTOM LINE

Do not simply copy Claude tape.
Do not simply summarize Reuters.
Do not turn Layer 6 into the final answer without audit.
V-BIS. EPS QUALITY GATE — MANDATORY

Before writing any final company block, explicitly check whether reported EPS / net income is materially affected by:
- non-operating investment gains or losses
- unrealized equity-security gains or losses
- tax benefits or tax-rate anomalies
- buybacks / share-count effects
- restructuring / litigation / impairment items
- acquisition accounting
- mark-to-market effects
- reserve releases or builds

If any item is material:
- flag it in HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE under EPS / Earnings
- include it in SECTOR KPI TABLE as a separate KPI row
- discuss it in OFFICIAL EARNINGS DETAIL
- make it central in COMMENT — ANALYST LAYER
- adjust PM_READ if it changes beat quality
- do not describe the EPS beat as clean

For mega-cap tech specifically, non-operating AI / private-market equity gains and tax benefits must be treated as EPS-quality issues, not as minor footnotes.
VI. QUALITY SCREEN BY SECTOR

Apply the correct sector lens.

Banks / Brokers:
- revenue by division
- NII vs fees vs trading
- IB pipeline
- FICC vs equities breadth
- provisions
- CET1 / RWA
- capital return
- tax rate / one-offs
- ROE / ROTE quality
- client activity
- financing intensity

Asset Managers:
- flows
- AUM / AUS
- fee rate
- performance fees
- operating leverage
- mix shift
- alternatives / private markets
- capital return

Software:
- revenue growth
- ARR / RPO / cRPO
- NRR / churn
- billings
- margin / FCF
- AI monetization
- seat vs consumption dynamics
- guide quality

Semiconductors:
- segment mix
- AI / hyperscaler exposure
- backlog
- inventory
- gross margin
- capex cycle
- China / export controls
- customer concentration
- guide credibility

Retail / Consumer:
- comps
- traffic vs ticket
- gross margin
- inventory
- promotions
- consumer cohort
- private label
- guide tone
- elasticity / trade-down

Industrials:
- orders
- backlog
- book-to-bill
- pricing vs volume
- margins
- supply chain
- capex cycle
- China / Europe / US exposure

Healthcare:
- volume / price / mix
- pipeline
- loss of exclusivity
- utilization
- MLR for managed care
- regulatory risk
- guidance quality

Energy:
- production
- realized price
- capex
- FCF
- buybacks / dividend
- leverage
- refining margins
- LNG / upstream / downstream mix

VII. FINAL COMPANY NOTE CONSTRUCTION RULE

Only after the intelligence tape and owner synthesis are complete, write the final company block using the locked format.

The final company note must be an owned synthesis, not a raw paste of the scout tape.

============================================================
HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE — GENERIC STREAMLIT RULE
============================================================

The HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE is mandatory for every full company note.

Purpose:
- provide a parser-stable PM compact view
- summarize the universal earnings result before detailed analysis
- allow Streamlit to compare companies across sectors
- avoid forcing the user to open the full note for the key headline result

This table is generic and must be valid for all stocks.

Column structure is locked:

| Metric | Actual | Consensus / Prior | Beat / Miss | YoY | QoQ | PM Comment |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|

Mandatory rows:

| Metric | Actual | Consensus / Prior | Beat / Miss | YoY | QoQ | PM Comment |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Revenue / Sales | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [comment] |
| EPS / Earnings | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [comment] |
| Profitability / Margin | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [comment] |
| Guidance / Outlook | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [comment] |
| Market reaction | [value] | — | [value] | — | — | [comment] |

Rules:
- rows must remain the same across all full company notes
- columns must never change
- this table is for cross-stock comparability
- use only verified data
- if a field is not relevant, write —
- if consensus is not confirmed, write Consensus not confirmed
- if market reaction is not confirmed, write Market reaction not confirmed
- do not invent beat / miss
- do not invent consensus
- do not insert unsupported price moves
- PM Comment must be short, analytical and PM-useful
- the table must be valid Markdown
- the separator line with |---| must always be present
- do not use HTML tables
- do not use decorative formatting
- do not use multi-line cells

============================================================
SECTOR KPI TABLE — SECTOR-SPECIFIC STREAMLIT RULE
============================================================

The SECTOR KPI TABLE is mandatory for every full company note when meaningful sector KPIs exist.

Purpose:
- capture the true business-specific earnings signal
- preserve sector-specific analytical depth
- avoid overloading the generic HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE
- allow Streamlit to display a second, more detailed sector-aware table

This table is flexible by sector.

Column structure is locked:

| KPI | Actual | Prior / Benchmark | Change | PM Comment |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|

Rules:
- columns must never change
- row names are flexible and sector-specific
- include 4 to 12 rows maximum
- use only verified data
- if prior / benchmark is unavailable, write —
- if change is not meaningful, write —
- PM Comment must be short and analytical
- the table must be valid Markdown
- the separator line with |---| must always be present
- do not use HTML tables
- do not use decorative formatting
- do not use multi-line cells

Sector-specific row examples:

US CONSUMER

[text]

[text]

<<SECTOR_BEGIN>>
SECTOR: [sector name]

...
<<SECTOR_END>>

[repeat sector blocks]

<<SECTOR_RECAP_END>>

THEME: [theme]
COMMENTARY: [short text]

...

<<KEY_CROSS_THEMES_END>>

<<EARNINGS_SEASON_RECAP_END>>

Rules for recap file:
- concise
- PM-readable
- grouped by sector
- derived from stock notes
- no duplicated long-form analysis
- short commentaries only in sector recap
- use PUBLICATION_DATE in all new recap lines
- legacy PUBLI_DATE may be read by Streamlit but should not be generated in new output

<<EARNINGS_RELEASES_BY_STOCK_BEGIN>>

FULL COMPANY NOTE STRUCTURE — LOCKED

Each company block must use:

<<[TICKER]_EARNINGS_BEGIN>>
TICKER: [ticker]
COMPANY: [full legal company name]
SECTOR: [stable broad sector label]
SUBSECTOR: [stable subsector label]
COUNTRY: [country]
PUBLICATION_DATE: [YYYY-MM-DD]
EVENT: [e.g. Q1 2026]
STATE_TRANSITION: [Improvement / Continuation / Stabilization / Reversal / Deterioration / False dawn / Mixed]
IMPORTANCE: [* / ** / *** / ****]
MARKET_REACTION: [Positive / Negative / Mixed / Neutral / Not confirmed]
MARKET_REACTION_DETAIL: [short anchored description]
PM_READ: [one-line PM read]
THEMES: [comma-separated themes]
SEGMENT_TABLE_STATUS: [Full / Partial / Not meaningful]
SOURCE_ROLE: [Full note / Brief note]

EXEC SUMMARY

HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE

SECTOR KPI TABLE

OFFICIAL EARNINGS DETAIL

SEGMENT / BUSINESS BREAKDOWN

GUIDANCE / CAPITAL ALLOCATION

PROFESSIONAL MARKET COMMENTARY

COMMENT — ANALYST LAYER

CONTEXT FROM PRIOR QUARTER / PRIOR DEBATE

HF TAKE — STRATEGIST LAYER

MARKET REACTION / PEER READ-ACROSS

KEY ISSUES TO MONITOR

BOTTOM LINE

<<[TICKER]_EARNINGS_END>>

HEADER FIELD RULES

The header must be parser-stable.

Rules:
- one metadata field per line
- use uppercase field names
- do not reorder fields
- do not add fields casually
- use PUBLICATION_DATE, not PUBLI_DATE, in all new output
- split SECTOR and SUBSECTOR
- MARKET_REACTION must be compact
- MARKET_REACTION_DETAIL must be one sentence maximum
- PM_READ must be one line maximum
- THEMES must be comma-separated
- SOURCE_ROLE allowed values: Full note / Brief note
- SEGMENT_TABLE_STATUS allowed values: Full / Partial / Not meaningful

MARKET_REACTION allowed values:
- Positive
- Negative
- Mixed
- Neutral
- Not confirmed

MARKET_REACTION_DETAIL examples:
- Stock up roughly 5% after-hours after revenue and guidance beat.
- Stock down roughly 3% pre-market despite EPS/revenue beat; reaction partly affected by broader risk-off session.
- Market reaction not confirmed at time of note construction.

PM_READ rule:
- one sentence
- direct PM implication
- must not be promotional
- must reflect both positive and negative quality points when relevant

EXEC SUMMARY RULE

EXEC SUMMARY is mandatory.

Purpose:
- create the bridge between sector recap and full note
- provide fast PM readability
- allow Streamlit preview rendering

Length:
- 3 to 5 lines maximum

It must answer:
- what happened
- what mattered
- what the PM read is

Preferred form:
- state transition
- one sentence on the quarter
- one sentence on the key signal
- one sentence on PM / stock implication

Example:
Improvement. Very strong franchise quarter, but low-cleanliness beat. Capital markets and equities delivered, while FICC, tax rate, capital intensity and provisions limited the rerating quality. PM read: the franchise signal improved, but investors still need broader desk participation and cleaner capital efficiency.

HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE RULE

HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE is mandatory immediately after EXEC SUMMARY.

Purpose:
- enable Streamlit PM Compact View
- provide a generic cross-stock snapshot
- avoid forcing the user to open the full note for the key result
- preserve comparability across companies and sectors

Use the locked Markdown structure:

HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE

| Metric | Actual | Consensus / Prior | Beat / Miss | YoY | QoQ | PM Comment |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|
| Revenue / Sales | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [comment] |
| EPS / Earnings | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [comment] |
| Profitability / Margin | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [comment] |
| Guidance / Outlook | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [comment] |
| Market reaction | [value] | — | [value] | — | — | [comment] |

Rules:
- rows must remain the same across all full company notes
- columns must never change
- use only verified numbers
- do not invent consensus
- do not invent beat / miss
- if not relevant, write —
- if consensus is missing, write Consensus not confirmed
- if market reaction is not confirmed, write Market reaction not confirmed
- PM Comment must be short, analytical and PM-useful
- the table must be valid Markdown with a separator row
- do not use HTML
- do not use decorative formatting
- do not use multi-line cells

SECTOR KPI TABLE RULE

SECTOR KPI TABLE appears immediately after HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE.

Purpose:
- capture sector-specific KPI detail
- preserve equity-desk analytical depth
- avoid making the headline table too sector-specific
- support Streamlit display of a second, more detailed table

Use the locked Markdown structure:

SECTOR KPI TABLE

| KPI | Actual | Prior / Benchmark | Change | PM Comment |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|
| [sector-specific KPI] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [short comment] |

Rules:
- columns must never change
- row names are flexible and sector-specific
- 4 to 12 rows maximum
- use only verified numbers
- do not invent benchmarks
- if prior / benchmark is unavailable, write —
- if change is not meaningful, write —
- PM Comment must be short and analytical
- the table must be valid Markdown with a separator row
- do not use HTML
- do not use decorative formatting
- do not use multi-line cells

If no meaningful sector KPI table can be built, write:

SECTOR KPI TABLE

Sector KPI table not meaningful for this release.

OFFICIAL EARNINGS DETAIL RULE

This section is the mechanical factual anchor.

Purpose:
- preserve the official earnings data in readable form
- support auditability
- provide detail behind the headline and sector KPI tables
- avoid mixing factual data with analytical interpretation

Rules:
- no stock opinion
- no unsupported interpretation
- only reported / clearly anchored data
- distinguish actual vs consensus vs prior where available
- do not invent consensus
- do not recompute surprises unless anchored
- do not repeat every item already shown in tables unless needed for auditability
- maintain a clean factual style

Preferred format:
Revenue / Sales:
Consensus:
EPS / Earnings:
Profitability / Margins:
Key KPI:
Guidance headline:
Capital allocation:
Other relevant official details:

SEGMENT / BUSINESS BREAKDOWN RULE

Purpose:
capture business mix and what drove the quarter.

Rules:
- use reported segment structure
- do not invent segment data
- do not mix official segments and sub-lines without clear labelling
- if disclosure is limited, summarize only what is reported
- if segment disclosure is meaningful, include a Markdown-clean SEGMENT TABLE
- if segment disclosure is not meaningful, do not force a fake table

SEGMENT TABLE RULE

When segment disclosure is meaningful, this section must include a parser-stable Markdown segment table.

Use this format exactly:

SEGMENT TABLE

| Segment | % of Total | Revenue | YoY Growth | Margin Trend | Key Commentary |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---|---|
| [segment] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] | [value] |

Rules:
- the table must be valid Markdown
- the separator line with |---| must always be present
- do not use images
- do not use decorative formatting
- do not use HTML tables
- do not use multi-line cells
- preserve the column order exactly
- row labels must follow the company’s reported segment structure where possible
- if using sub-lines, label them clearly
- do not invent margins where not disclosed
- if % of total is computed, it must be simple arithmetic from verified segment revenue and group revenue

SEGMENT_TABLE_STATUS rules:
- Full = meaningful segment disclosure available and table included
- Partial = limited but useful disclosure available and table included
- Not meaningful = no meaningful segment disclosure; table may be omitted

COMMENTARY

After the segment table, include a short synthesis paragraph or short block explaining what matters most in the mix.

GUIDANCE / CAPITAL ALLOCATION RULE

Purpose:
capture what management said about the future and capital deployment.

Include where relevant:
- next quarter guide
- full-year guide
- revenue / EPS / margin guide
- capex
- buybacks
- dividend
- M&A
- restructuring
- investment intensity
- RWA / CET1 / balance sheet deployment for banks
- backlog / pipeline

Keep this section mostly mechanical.
Interpretation belongs later.

If no formal guide:
No formal numeric guidance provided.

PROFESSIONAL MARKET COMMENTARY RULE

This is the institutional tape summary.

Purpose:
capture the professional narrative around the quarter.

Sources in order of priority:
- Claude tape
- official management framing
- Reuters / Bloomberg / institutional media
- public professional commentary
- optional additional scout material

Allowed content:
- beat / miss framing
- quality of revenue
- margin narrative
- guide tone
- AI / macro / product-cycle framing
- stock reaction logic
- peer read-across already visible in the tape

Section must stay compact.

Must distinguish:
- official management framing
- journalist / wire framing
- public professional commentary
- lower-confidence narrative signals

COMMENT — ANALYST LAYER RULE

This is the analytical core.

Allowed content:
- beat quality vs headline
- segment hierarchy
- margin bridge
- guidance credibility
- growth durability
- backlog / bookings / pipeline quality
- one-off vs recurring drivers
- capital intensity
- tax / accounting / provision quality
- what matters more than the headline
- why the stock may react differently from the print

Mandatory line:
State transition: [value]

Allowed values only:
- Improvement
- Continuation
- Stabilization
- Reversal
- Deterioration
- False dawn
- Mixed

CONTEXT FROM PRIOR QUARTER / PRIOR DEBATE RULE

This paragraph is mandatory.

Maximum:
- 3 sentences

It must contain only:
- prior trajectory
- how the new print confirms / changes / weakens it
- one implication for thesis continuity

No process language.
No sourcing-debugging language.
No meta-commentary.

HF TAKE — STRATEGIST LAYER RULE

Purpose:
map the quarter to the stock reaction function.

Allowed content:
- what the market is pricing
- whether the reaction makes sense
- multiple implications
- positioning / expectation asymmetry
- peer read-across
- what has to happen next for rerating
- what would break the thesis
- next verification tests

Use conditional language.
Avoid exaggerated regime calls from one quarter.

MARKET REACTION / PEER READ-ACROSS RULE

Purpose:
place the print inside the broader sector / peer setup.

Include where relevant:
- immediate stock reaction
- premarket / postmarket move
- peer sympathy moves
- sector implications
- supplier / customer read-through

Only include anchored reaction data.
Do not invent price moves.

If no reliable move:
Market reaction not confirmed at time of note construction.

KEY ISSUES TO MONITOR RULE

Format:

[Issue]
Why it matters: [1–3 lines]

[Issue]
Why it matters: [1–3 lines]

[Issue]
Why it matters: [1–3 lines]

Selection criteria:
- strongest stock relevance
- strongest uncertainty
- strongest implication for next quarter
- strongest macro / PM read-across if relevant

Use 3 issues maximum unless the user asks for more.

BOTTOM LINE RULE

Must be concise.

It should answer:
- was the quarter actually good or bad?
- why did the stock react that way?
- what is the single most important thing to monitor next?

============================================================
STREAMLIT PM COMPACT VIEW — TARGET RENDERING LOGIC
============================================================

The stock block must allow Streamlit to render a clean PM Compact View without opening the full institutional note.

Streamlit should be able to extract:

1. Header card
   - Ticker
   - Company
   - Sector
   - Subsector
   - Country
   - Event
   - Publication date
   - Importance
   - State transition
   - Market reaction

2. PM_READ
   - direct one-line PM implication from header

3. EXEC SUMMARY
   - 3–5 line preview

4. HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE
   - generic cross-stock table
   - always displayed first
   - same rows for every company

5. SECTOR KPI TABLE
   - sector-specific detailed KPI table
   - displayed second
   - rows vary by sector

6. SEGMENT TABLE
   - render as dataframe / Markdown table when available

7. WHAT CHANGED / WHAT MATTERS NEXT
   - pull from COMMENT — ANALYST LAYER or KEY ISSUES TO MONITOR

8. SHORT HF TAKE
   - pull first compact paragraph from HF TAKE — STRATEGIST LAYER

9. FULL INSTITUTIONAL NOTE
   - expander containing all remaining sections

Generator implication:
- HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE must always exist in full notes
- SECTOR KPI TABLE must exist when sector KPIs are meaningful
- SEGMENT TABLE must be valid Markdown when present
- OFFICIAL EARNINGS DETAIL replaces REPORTED FACTS
- metadata fields must be complete
- PM_READ must be directly usable as card text
- MARKET_REACTION_DETAIL must be directly usable as card subtitle

PARSER STABILITY RULES

Because files are saved as .txt and read by Streamlit:
- never change markers casually
- never rename major sections
- never reorder sections
- metadata must remain one field per line
- use ISO dates only: YYYY-MM-DD
- use text tables only
- use Markdown separator rows for tables
- do not rely on images
- do not rely on decorative markdown
- do not use inconsistent synonyms for stable metadata fields
- do not use PUBLI_DATE in new output; use PUBLICATION_DATE
- for legacy support only, Streamlit may read PUBLI_DATE as fallback

SECTOR LABEL STABILITY RULE

Use stable sector naming across the season.
Do not rename sectors casually.

In v2.3:
- SECTOR = broad sector
- SUBSECTOR = more precise business label

Examples:

SECTOR: Financials
SUBSECTOR: Investment Banking & Markets

SECTOR: Financials
SUBSECTOR: Banking

SECTOR: Financials
SUBSECTOR: Consumer Finance & Payments

SECTOR: Semiconductors
SUBSECTOR: Foundry

SECTOR: Semiconductors
SUBSECTOR: AI Infrastructure

SECTOR: Software
SUBSECTOR: Cloud & Applications

SECTOR: Industrials
SUBSECTOR: Aerospace & Defense

SECTOR: Consumer Staples
SUBSECTOR: Household & Personal Care

SECTOR: Consumer Discretionary
SUBSECTOR: Restaurants

SECTOR: Industrials
SUBSECTOR: Machinery

SECTOR: Healthcare
SUBSECTOR: Managed Care

COUNTRY RULE

COUNTRY must always be explicit.
Do not infer silently.
Use one stable country label per company.

STATE TRANSITION RULE

Every full company block must include one state transition.

Allowed values only:
- Improvement
- Continuation
- Stabilization
- Reversal
- Deterioration
- False dawn
- Mixed

Definitions:

Improvement
- print strengthens the prior debate or marks a real positive shift

Continuation
- print confirms existing trajectory without major new information

Stabilization
- prior weakness stops worsening, but no full improvement yet

Reversal
- print reverses a prior trend meaningfully

Deterioration
- print weakens the thesis or confirms negative pressure

False dawn
- headline looks better but quality / guide / mix does not support it

Mixed
- major positive and negative signals coexist, with no clean direction

OUTPUT RULE

When the user asks for:
- the scout list → return the current important names to scout
- the stock note → return the full current company block
- the season recap → return the current recap
- a refresh read-across → update the recap from the stock notes
- a sector view → use the recap-style sector grouping
- a PM compact view → return header + PM_READ + EXEC SUMMARY + HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE + SECTOR KPI TABLE + SEGMENT TABLE + short HF take

Only provide patch-only output if explicitly requested.

If the user provides a scout tape and asks to write the stock block:
- ingest the scout
- verify key official facts if needed
- apply the Earnings Event Intelligence Module
- produce the full company block unless patch-only is requested
- include HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE
- include SECTOR KPI TABLE when sector KPIs are meaningful
- include Markdown SEGMENT TABLE when meaningful
- use OFFICIAL EARNINGS DETAIL instead of REPORTED FACTS
- use the v2.3 enriched header

If the user provides a weak prior stock block:
- audit it against the module
- identify missing facts / weak synthesis
- rewrite the block in locked structure if requested

FINAL OPERATING PRINCIPLE

This process must function as a live earnings intelligence system.

It must allow the user to:
- know which names matter enough to scout
- track what actually printed
- separate facts from narrative
- understand what matters inside the quarter
- compare the print to prior debate
- distinguish headline surprise from quality of surprise
- maintain one source-of-truth file by stock
- maintain one season-level PM recap file
- support a GitHub / Streamlit workflow without structure drift
- render a PM Compact View from metadata + headline earnings table + sector KPI table + segment table

The final standard is:

Official facts fixed.
Narrative evidence gated.
Scout tape used but not obeyed blindly.
Owner synthesis required.
Generic headline earnings table mandatory.
Sector KPI table mandatory when meaningful.
Markdown segment table mandatory where meaningful.
Official earnings detail replaces reported facts.
Final stock block parser-stable.
Season recap derived from stock blocks only.

Thought for 4s
Template ingested and will be the operative workflow for this earnings-season chat.

I will apply v2.3 with:

one season / one reporting window

two txt outputs only:

EARNINGS_SEASON_RECAP_[SEASON].txt

EARNINGS_RELEASES_BY_STOCK_[SEASON].txt

mandatory SCOUT_TRACKER

mandatory Earnings Event Intelligence Module before each final stock block

mandatory web anchoring for every earnings event

PUBLICATION_DATE only for new notes

enriched header with SECTOR / SUBSECTOR, MARKET_REACTION, PM_READ

mandatory HEADLINE EARNINGS TABLE

mandatory SECTOR KPI TABLE when meaningful

Markdown-clean SEGMENT TABLE when meaningful

OFFICIAL EARNINGS DETAIL, not REPORTED FACTS

season recap derived only from validated stock blocks

Send me either the season/window to initialize the two files, or the first stock / scout tape / earnings release to process.


do those with scout
[JPM — JPMORGAN CHASE — Q1 2026]
Release: 2026-04-14 | Pre-market

LAYER 0 — OFFICIAL / MECHANICAL EARNINGS BASE
Net income $16.5B (+13% YoY from $14.6B). Diluted EPS $5.94 (+17% YoY; beat consensus $5.49 by 8%). Managed net revenue $50.5B (+10% YoY; beat consensus ~$49B). ROTCE 23%. ROE 19%. Tickeron
Segment breakdown:

CIB revenue $23.4B (+19% YoY): record Markets $11.6B (+20%), IB fees $2.88B (+28%). CCB revenue $19.6B (+7%). AWM revenue $6.4B (+11%), AUM $4.8T. Tickeron
NII $25.5B (+9% YoY). Noninterest revenue $25.1B (+11%). Avg. loans $1.5T (+11% YoY). Avg. deposits $2.6T (+7% YoY). Quartr
Expenses $26.9B (+14% YoY) — higher compensation, front office headcount, brokerage/distribution costs, absence of prior year FDIC accrual release. Credit costs $2.5B: NCOs $2.3B + reserve build $191M. CET1 14.3% (−30bps QoQ as capital distributions + higher RWA exceeded net income). The Motley Fool

Capital returned: $4.1B dividends + $8.1B buybacks. Tickeron
FY 2026 guidance: NII ex-Markets ~$95B; total NII ~$103B (trimmed from $104.5B prior). Adjusted expenses ~$105B. Card NCO rate ~3.4%. AlphaSense
Consensus beat/miss: EPS +8%; revenue +3%. NII guide trim to $103B from $104.5B the primary negative.
Source: SEC 8-K (official); JPM press release; confirmed readable. Reliability: High

LAYER 1 — OFFICIAL ENRICHMENT
CEO Jamie Dimon (press release): "Performance was strong across our businesses. In the CIB, revenue grew 19%. Markets revenue reached a record $11.6 billion, while IB fees increased 28% due to stronger advisory and ECM activity. Additionally, Payments continued to deliver very strong results. In CCB, revenue rose 7%. We continued to acquire new customers at a robust rate across the franchise, including achieving record net inflows in self-directed investing and opening more than 450,000 net new checking accounts. Finally, in AWM, revenue increased 11%." JPMorgan Chase
On macro risks (call): Dimon issued "sobering warnings regarding a 'complex set of global risks'" on the earnings call. FinancialContent
On Basel III / G-SIB: Management estimates Basel III endgame proposals would require a 4% increase in CET1 capital for JPM. G-SIB surcharge expected to increase to 5.2% in 2028 (+70bps from 4.5%), implying ~$20B additional GSIB capital. Management stated: "It is very hard to reconcile the principles articulated in the 2015 Fed G-SIB white paper with an outcome where JPMorgan Chase has $109 billion of G-SIB surcharge." The Motley Fool
On NII guide trim: NII ex-Markets ~$95B maintained; total NII trimmed to $103B (from $104.5B) as Markets NII expected to decrease to ~$8B due to rates, "primarily offset in net interest revenue." AlphaSense
On private credit: JPM's private credit exposure ~$50B (portion of $160B core NBFI exposure involving leveraged loan investors). Management does not believe private credit defaults would be systemic, but expects some players in private credit "will not be particularly good at it and that business may come back to banks." AlphaSense
On data centre lending: Markets loan growth "will be opportunistic, particularly in data center lending and related businesses, with willingness to walk away if terms do not make sense." AlphaSense
Compensation ratio and tax rate: Both lower than expected per Barclays, alongside the larger buyback — contributing to the quality of the EPS beat. FinancialContent
Source: SEC 8-K, Motley Fool transcript, CNBC, Alpha-Sense call summary. Reliability: High

LAYER 2A — ACCESSIBLE COMMENTARY
FinancialContent / MarketMinute: "JPMorgan Chase kicked off the first-quarter earnings season today, delivering a significant performance beat that momentarily silenced skeptics. The banking giant reported an adjusted EPS of $5.94, comfortably outpacing the analyst consensus of $5.46. Total revenue reached a staggering $50.5 billion... However, the market's initial cheer was quickly dampened by a cautious revision to the bank's full-year outlook for Net Interest Income (NII). Despite the headline growth, shares of the nation's largest lender slipped nearly 3% in early trading." FinancialContent
Broader sector read-across signalled: "The shift in NII guidance suggests that other traditional lenders like Wells Fargo and Bank of America may face similar pressure on their lending margins... Conversely, the strength in JPMorgan's investment banking and trading arms bodes well for pure-play investment banks such as Goldman Sachs and Morgan Stanley." FinancialContent
Stock reaction: Shares dipped ~1%–3% post-earnings, "pressured by the trimmed NII outlook signaling deposit competition and rate sensitivity." Tickeron
Reliability: High

LAYER 2B — INSTITUTIONAL / HOUSE VIEW
Barclays: Lower-than-expected comp ratio, lower tax rate, and larger-than-expected buyback contributed to the EPS beat quality. The NII trim is genuine, not a reporting artefact.
Sector bellwether read: JPM's NII guide trim to $103B (from $104.5B) sent an immediate signal to WFC and BAC that lending margin headwinds were real — confirmed when WFC subsequently reported NIM compression and NII sequential decline.
Basel III/G-SIB overhang: Management flagging $20B+ additional capital requirement from regulatory evolution is a significant medium-term constraint on capital return flexibility. This is the primary structural headwind in the JPM forward narrative.
Reliability: High

LAYER 3 — NARRATIVE SIGNALS
Signal 1: Record Markets ($11.6B, +20%) and IB fees +28% — the same M&A and ECM recovery that benefited GS is flowing through JPM's CIB. The investment banking revival is broad-based, not Goldman-specific. Reliability: High
Signal 2: NII guide trimmed from $104.5B to $103B — this is $1.5B of annual NII being removed from forecasts. The stated driver is Markets NII declining on rates, "primarily offset in fee income." The market correctly identified this as the operative negative signal; it set the tone for WFC's sequential NII decline to land as a confirmation, not a surprise. Reliability: High
Signal 3: Expense growth +14% vs. revenue +10% — negative operating leverage in Q1. Management explicitly stated the $105B expense guide is "contingent on business results rather than a fixed target" — i.e., expenses will grow if revenues grow. This removes the floor under expense discipline. Reliability: High
Signal 4: Stock −1%–3% on a significant beat — the market is penalising the NII guide trim and basiline capital concerns more than rewarding the clean operational outperformance. Setup problem: JPM entered Q1 at near all-time highs with very high expectations. Reliability: High

LAYER 5 — NARRATIVE CLUSTERS
Cluster 1: "IB recovery confirmed; Markets still the engine"
Record CIB of $23.4B (+19%) with Markets at $11.6B and IB fees +28%. The JPM CIB print is the definitive confirmation that the investment banking cycle is in genuine recovery.
Confidence: High
Cluster 2: "NII headwind is the sector-wide signal"
$103B total NII guidance (down from $104.5B) reflects the reality that higher-for-longer rates are no longer a clear NII tailwind as deposit repricing eats into margins. The trim cascaded into WFC and BAC narratives immediately.
Confidence: High
Cluster 3: "Basel/G-SIB capital overhang"
Dimon's repeated emphasis on Basel III endgame and G-SIB surcharge ($109B total) signals that regulatory capital requirements are the binding constraint on JPM's capital return trajectory. The $20B incremental capital requirement from proposed changes is the medium-term headwind.
Confidence: High

LAYER 6 — NARRATIVE VS DATA DIVERGENCE
Data: Second-highest-ever quarterly revenue. Record Markets. ROTCE 23%. EPS +17%. $12.2B returned to shareholders.
Narrative: Dominated by the $1.5B NII guide trim and Dimon's macro warnings. The "bellwether" function of JPM's earnings means the forward guidance signal outweighs the backward-looking beat in market impact.
Divergence: Moderate — the NII trim is real and material as a sector signal, but the magnitude of the narrative weight placed on it (−3% stock, sector-wide re-rating) is somewhat disproportionate to the actual $1.5B trim versus a $50.5B revenue base.

LAYER 2A — ACCESSIBLE COMMENTARY

The annualized net interest income from Q1 ($48.4 billion) is already below the full-year target, implying that a significant reversal of the current margin compression is needed to meet the goal. Similarly, the annualized expense run-rate ($57.3 billion) is well above the full-year guidance, suggesting that substantial cost-cutting measures or a slowdown in investment spending will be required." SignalBloom AI

LAYER 2B — INSTITUTIONAL / HOUSE VIEW
Key analytical concern: WFC is growing its loan book (+10% YoY) but the yield on that growth is being compressed by deposit repricing and a growing lower-margin markets balance sheet. The result is NII growing only 5% YoY despite 10% loan growth — and then the first sequential NII decline in over a year in Q1. This is the core structural tension in the WFC thesis.
Annualised NII run-rate gap: Q1 NII of $12.096B annualises to ~$48.4B — below the $50B FY target. Management's confidence in the $50B requires NII acceleration through Q2–Q4 (i.e., recovery from the 2-fewer-days effect, rate re-pricing favourably, and NIM stabilising). This is achievable but requires execution.
Expense run-rate gap: Q1 expense of $14.33B annualises to ~$57.3B — above the $55.7B FY target. Requires deceleration in H2.
Reliability: High

LAYER 3 — NARRATIVE SIGNALS
Signal 1: NII sequential decline of −$235M QoQ — first in over a year. On the same day JPM trimmed its NII guide, WFC delivered an actual sequential NII decline. This is the negative combination that drove the −5% stock reaction despite the headline EPS beat. Reliability: High
Signal 2: NIM −13bps QoQ to 2.47% — fourth consecutive quarterly decline. The trajectory is not yet reversing; management expects additional near-term compression. This is a persistent structural headwind, not a one-quarter anomaly. Reliability: High
Signal 3: Revenue miss ($21.45B vs. $21.79B consensus) — the miss is driven entirely by NII softness; noninterest income (+8%) was actually positive. This is a rate/margin story, not a volume or fee story. Reliability: High
Signal 4: EPS beat on tax items ($0.04/share from prior period resolution) — the headline EPS beat is partly a quality concern. Ex-tax benefit, EPS would have been $1.56 — below consensus. Reliability: High
Signal 5: All five segments grew revenue 7%–14% — the fee and volume growth is real and broad-based. The problem is structural, not operational. Reliability: High

LAYER 5 — NARRATIVE CLUSTERS
Cluster 1: "NII compression is the binding constraint"
Sequential NII decline (-$235M), NIM -13bps (4th consecutive quarterly decline), annualised Q1 run rate below full-year target — the NII story is the dominant negative narrative and it has not bottomed yet.
Confidence: High
Cluster 2: "Expense run-rate above guidance is an underappreciated risk"
Q1 annualised expenses of ~$57.3B vs $55.7B FY target requires meaningful H2 deceleration. The asset cap removal removes the primary cost headwind but marketing/tech investment is accelerating.

LAYER 6 — NARRATIVE VS DATA DIVERGENCE
Data: EPS +15% YoY. Revenue +6% YoY. All segments growing. Loans >$1T. FY NII guide maintained at $50B. $4B returned to shareholders.
Narrative: Dominated by NII sequential decline (−$235M), NIM −13bps (4th quarterly decline), revenue miss, and the observation that the annualised Q1 NII run-rate and expense run-rate are both on the wrong side of FY guidance. The market penalised the print −5% despite the headline EPS beat.
Divergence: Moderate — the divergence is between a genuine operational improvement story (volume, fees, segments) and a structural margin compression reality (NIM −4 consecutive quarters, NII sequential decline). The market is correctly weighting the forward NII signal over the backward EPS beat. However, management's confidence in the $50B NII target (requiring NII growth in Q2–Q4) is the thesis test for the remainder of 2026.

State transition: Stabilization — WFC's operational franchise is improving across all segments; loan growth is real; fee income is growing. But the NIM compression and first sequential NII decline in over a year are structural headwinds that override the EPS beat narrative. The $50B full-year NII target requires a H2 NII acceleration that is achievable but not certain. Capital-markets durability

Macro risk commentary

OFFICIAL EARNINGS DETAIL

Revenue / Sales:
Managed revenue was $50.5B, up 10% YoY. Net interest income was $25.5B, up 9% YoY. Noninterest revenue was $25.1B, up 11% YoY.

Consensus:
Consensus was roughly $49.0B for revenue and $5.49 for EPS. JPM beat on both headline revenue and EPS.

EPS / Earnings:
Net income was $16.5B, up 13% YoY. Diluted EPS was $5.94, up 17% YoY.

Profitability / Margins:
ROTCE was 23%, ROE was 19%, and the managed overhead ratio was 53%. Expense was $26.9B, up 14% YoY, outpacing revenue growth.

Key KPI:
CIB revenue was $23.4B, up 19% YoY. Markets revenue was a record $11.6B, up 20% YoY. Investment banking fees were $2.88B, up 28% YoY. AWM revenue was $6.4B, up 11% YoY, with AUM of $4.8T.

Guidance headline:
FY2026 total NII guidance was reduced to approximately $103B, while NII excluding Markets was maintained at approximately $95B. Adjusted expenses are expected at approximately $105B.

Capital allocation:
JPM returned $12.2B to shareholders through $4.1B of common dividends and $8.1B of common-stock net repurchases. Standardized CET1 was 14.3%, down 30bps QoQ.

Other relevant official details:
Credit costs were $2.5B, including $2.3B of net charge-offs and a $191M reserve build. JPM also flagged ongoing Basel III / G-SIB capital issues, with proposed regulatory changes still a medium-term capital-efficiency overhang.

SEGMENT TABLE

COMMENTARY

The quarter was led by CIB, not by a classic bank NII story. Markets, IB fees, Payments and AWM all confirmed that JPM’s diversified franchise can offset a softer forward NII slope, but the market reaction shows that investors still treat NII guidance as the binding large-bank variable.

GUIDANCE / CAPITAL ALLOCATION

FY2026 NII guidance was the decisive forward item. Total NII was guided to approximately $103B, down from the prior ~$104.5B marker, while NII excluding Markets remained around $95B. Adjusted expenses were guided at approximately $105B and the card services NCO rate at approximately 3.4%.

Capital return was large, with $12.2B distributed to common shareholders. However, standardized CET1 fell to 14.3%, and the Basel III / G-SIB discussion remains important because any higher required capital would reduce future buyback flexibility.

PROFESSIONAL MARKET COMMENTARY

The professional tape framed JPM as a strong operational beat with a forward guide problem. Record Markets, strong CIB and high ROTCE were widely acknowledged, but the stock reaction was capped by the NII guide reduction and Dimon’s cautious macro language.

The sector read-across was immediate: JPM’s NII guide trim raised the burden of proof for rate-sensitive lenders, while the CIB / Markets strength supported Goldman, Morgan Stanley and Citi-style capital-markets recovery narratives.

Lower-confidence narrative signals also pointed to high starting expectations: JPM entered the print with a premium multiple and strong share-price momentum, so even a high-quality beat was not enough once the forward NII slope moved lower.

COMMENT — ANALYST LAYER

The headline quarter was excellent, but the stock was never going to trade only the backward-looking EPS beat. JPM’s real signal is that the bank can still generate near-peak profitability through CIB, Markets, Payments and AWM even as NII becomes less linear.

The highest-quality part of the print was CIB breadth: IB fees up 28%, Markets at a record $11.6B, Payments up 12%, and AWM AUM at $4.8T. The lowest-quality part was not credit; it was the combination of NII guide trim, expense growth above revenue growth, and capital/regulatory friction.

State transition: Improvement

CONTEXT FROM PRIOR QUARTER / PRIOR DEBATE

The prior debate was whether JPM could remain the cleanest large-bank compounder as the NII windfall normalized. This quarter confirms that capital markets, banking fees, Payments and AWM can carry the earnings mix. The thesis remains intact, but the driver is now less NII beta and more diversified fee / markets durability.

HF TAKE — STRATEGIST LAYER

The reaction makes sense: for a premium bank, the market needs not only a beat but also a clean forward slope. JPM delivered the beat, but the NII guide trim reduced the forward compounding clarity.

The stock should keep its quality premium if CIB strength persists and credit remains benign. The risk is that volatility and deal activity fade while the NII guide moves lower, leaving the market with peak-ish returns, higher expenses and more capital-regulatory debate.

The next rerating test is not whether JPM is a great bank. It is whether fee and markets strength can remain durable enough to offset the fading NII windfall without forcing expense and RWA intensity materially higher.

MARKET REACTION / PEER READ-ACROSS

The stock traded down despite the EPS and revenue beat because investors focused on the NII guide cut and the forward return composition. Relative to GS, JPM had broader balance and stronger FICC / banking breadth; relative to WFC, JPM had a much cleaner fee and markets offset to NII pressure.

Peer read-across: CIB and capital-markets recovery were positive for GS, MS and C; NII guide pressure was negative for WFC and BAC-style spread lenders.

KEY ISSUES TO MONITOR

NII slope
Why it matters: The total NII guide cut was the main reason the market faded the beat.

CIB durability
Why it matters: Markets and investment banking now need to carry more of the earnings mix as NII becomes less supportive.

Capital and G-SIB pressure
Why it matters: Higher required capital would reduce the flexibility of JPM’s buyback and capital-return story.

BOTTOM LINE

Excellent quarter, but not a clean rerating print.
The stock reacted negatively because the forward NII guide mattered more than the backward-looking EPS beat.
The next issue is whether CIB, Payments and AWM can keep offsetting the NII normalization without excessive expense and capital intensity.

EPS / Earnings:
Net income was $5.8B, up 42% YoY. Diluted EPS was $3.06, up 56% YoY.

Profitability / Margins:
RoTCE was 13.1%, above Citi’s 10% to 11% full-year target range. ROE was 11.5%. The efficiency ratio was approximately 58%, improved by roughly 410bps YoY.

Key KPI:

Guidance headline:

Other relevant official details:

COMMENTARY

Citi’s quarter was more than a volatility-assisted trading beat. Services generated 27% RoTCE, firmwide RoTCE exceeded the full-year target, and management maintained 2026 guidance. That is why the market treated Citi differently from JPM and WFC: the print strengthened the transformation narrative rather than raising a new NII question.

GUIDANCE / CAPITAL ALLOCATION

Management maintained the key 2026 targets: NII ex-Markets growth of 5% to 6%, efficiency ratio around 60%, U.S. Cards NCL rate of 4.0% to 4.5%, and RoTCE of 10% to 11%. The first quarter is seasonally strong, so management did not convert the 13.1% RoTCE print into a higher full-year target.

Capital return was meaningful, with $6.3B of share repurchases in Q1 and management reiterating that repurchases in 2026 should be higher than in 2025. The capital story remains central to the peer-discount compression case.

PROFESSIONAL MARKET COMMENTARY

The professional tape framed Citi as the clearest improvement story among the April 14 banks. Reuters highlighted the highest quarterly revenue in a decade, trading-driven strength, 13.1% RoTCE versus a 10% to 11% annual target, and Fraser’s message that the bank remains focused on organic growth.

The institutional narrative is shifting: Citi is no longer only a restructuring milestone story. It is beginning to show measurable return progress, positive operating leverage and a clearer capital-return path.

The residual skepticism is sustainability. Q1 is usually seasonally strong for capital markets, and management itself did not over-extrapolate the quarterly RoTCE into full-year guidance.

COMMENT — ANALYST LAYER

The highest-quality part of the print was Services. A 27% RoTCE business with deposit, cross-border and custody scale gives Citi a differentiated earnings base that is less dependent on U.S. consumer NII than a traditional spread lender.

The second key quality point was guidance stability. On the same day JPM trimmed total NII guidance and WFC printed a sequential NII decline, Citi maintained NII ex-Markets growth of 5% to 6%. That made Citi the positive NII divergence within the cohort.

The lowest-quality caveat is that Markets strength and Q1 seasonality helped the quarter. The market should not assume that 13.1% RoTCE is automatically the new run-rate until Citi repeats the performance through weaker seasonal periods.

State transition: Improvement

CONTEXT FROM PRIOR QUARTER / PRIOR DEBATE

The prior debate was whether Jane Fraser’s restructuring could translate into real returns rather than only simplification milestones. This print says yes: RoTCE moved above target, efficiency improved and Services remains structurally strong. The debate now shifts from transformation credibility to return durability.

HF TAKE — STRATEGIST LAYER

Citi was the cleanest positive surprise in the bank cohort because the print attacked the bear case directly. The bear case was that restructuring would take too long, returns would remain subscale and the peer discount would persist. Q1 showed returns above target, a stronger Services franchise and an active buyback.

The stock can continue to rerate if Services stays strong, Wealth keeps improving, and management uses Investor Day to raise confidence in medium-term returns. The risk is that Q1 proves too capital-markets-heavy and that the 13.1% RoTCE print fades back toward the 10% to 11% target without a higher medium-term ambition.

The tactical setup is constructive but less asymmetric after the move: the next catalyst is whether management can turn this quarter into a higher-quality medium-term return framework.

MARKET REACTION / PEER READ-ACROSS

Citi outperformed the April 14 bank cohort because its print had the best narrative/data alignment. JPM beat but cut total NII guidance; WFC beat EPS but missed revenue and showed NII / NIM compression. Citi beat, reaffirmed NII ex-Markets guidance and delivered RoTCE above target.

Peer read-across: Citi supports the capital-markets recovery narrative, but its more important read-across is that transformation stories can rerate when returns and capital return finally show up in the numbers.

KEY ISSUES TO MONITOR

Return durability
Why it matters: One quarter above target is important; repetition would make the peer-discount compression case more durable.

Services momentum
Why it matters: Services is the structural crown jewel and the highest-quality part of the franchise.

Investor Day / medium-term targets
Why it matters: The stock’s next rerating leg likely requires management to convert Q1 execution into a more credible medium-term return corridor.

BOTTOM LINE

Very strong quarter and the cleanest positive divergence in the April 14 bank cohort.
The stock reacted well because the numbers validated the transformation thesis rather than just beating estimates.
The next question is whether Citi can convert Q1’s above-target returns into a durable medium-term return reset.

Consensus was approximately $21.76B for revenue and $1.58 for EPS. Wells missed revenue and beat EPS by $0.02.

EPS / Earnings:
Net income was $5.253B, up 7% YoY. Diluted EPS was $1.60, up 15% YoY. The quarter included $135M, or $0.04 per share, of discrete tax benefits related to prior-period resolutions.

Profitability / Margins:
ROTCE was 14.5%, unchanged QoQ and up from 13.6% YoY. ROE was 12.2%. Net interest margin fell to 2.47%, down from 2.60% in Q4 2025 and 2.67% in Q1 2025. The efficiency ratio was 67%.

Key KPI:
Average loans were $996.0B, up 10% YoY, and average deposits were $1.415T, up 6% YoY. Revenue growth was broad across operating segments, but the NII and NIM trajectory weakened.

Guidance headline:
Management maintained FY2026 NII guidance around $50B and noninterest expense guidance around $55.7B.

Capital allocation:
Wells repurchased 46.3M shares, or $4.0B, in Q1 2026. CET1 was 10.3%, down from 11.1% one year earlier.

Other relevant official details:
Provision for credit losses was $1.135B, including $1.106B of NCOs and a $29M allowance build. Net charge-offs were 45bps annualized.

SEGMENT TABLE

COMMENTARY

The segment picture is better than the stock reaction suggests: all major operating segments showed revenue growth, WIM was strong, and loans are nearly at the $1T average balance threshold. The problem is translation. Loan and deposit growth are not yet converting into clean NII acceleration because NIM continues to compress.

GUIDANCE / CAPITAL ALLOCATION

Management maintained the FY2026 NII guide around $50B, which is better than a guide cut but still requires improvement versus the Q1 annualized run-rate. Q1 NII of $12.096B annualizes to roughly $48.4B, below the full-year guide, so the market needs to see sequential NII growth in the remaining quarters.

Expense guidance was also maintained around $55.7B, while Q1 noninterest expense of $14.330B annualizes above that level. This means the guide requires expense deceleration later in the year.

Capital return remained active with $4.0B of repurchases. CET1 at 10.3% remains adequate, but the buffer is lower than one year ago.

PROFESSIONAL MARKET COMMENTARY

The professional tape framed Wells as an earnings beat with weak quality. Reuters and public market commentary focused on the revenue miss, NII below expectations, NIM compression and stock decline.

The scout tape correctly identifies the core tension: Wells is growing loans and deposits, but the incremental balance-sheet growth is arriving at compressed margins. The market therefore treated the NII trajectory as more important than the headline EPS beat.

The positive narrative is that operational growth is real. The negative narrative is that Wells still has to prove that asset-cap normalization and balance-sheet growth can translate into higher-quality revenue.

COMMENT — ANALYST LAYER

This was not a deterioration quarter because the franchise is visibly growing: average loans were up 10%, deposits were up 6%, all major operating segments showed revenue growth, and WIM grew 14%. But it was not a clean improvement quarter either because the revenue miss and NII decline are exactly where investors are most focused.

The highest-quality part of the print was broad operating growth, especially WIM and balance-sheet expansion. The lowest-quality part was the EPS beat: a $0.04 discrete tax benefit means underlying EPS quality was weaker than the headline, while NIM fell again.

The maintained $50B NII guide is the key support. It prevents a full deterioration call, but it is now a test rather than a proof point.

State transition: Stabilization

CONTEXT FROM PRIOR QUARTER / PRIOR DEBATE

The prior debate was whether Wells could convert asset-cap normalization and balance-sheet growth into cleaner earnings growth. This print shows franchise growth but not yet clean monetization. The thesis remains alive, but the burden of proof has shifted to sequential NII and NIM stabilization.

HF TAKE — STRATEGIST LAYER

The stock reaction was rational. Investors did not punish Wells because the whole franchise is weak; they punished it because the most important line for a spread-sensitive bank moved the wrong way sequentially.

The upside case is still present: if loan growth persists, deposit costs stabilize, NII grows through Q2 to Q4, and expense run-rate improves, the stock can recover because the operating base is no longer impaired. But until the NII inflection is visible in reported numbers, the market will fade EPS beats that depend on tax benefits or arrive with revenue misses.

The next verification test is simple: NII must move up sequentially and NIM compression must slow. Without that, the recovery narrative remains stabilization, not improvement.

MARKET REACTION / PEER READ-ACROSS

Wells traded down around 5% because the market prioritized revenue quality, NII decline and NIM compression over the headline EPS beat. In the April 14 bank cohort, Wells was the clearest negative spread-bank read.

Peer read-across: JPM’s NII guide trim and Wells’ sequential NII decline together confirm that NII is no longer a uniform tailwind. Citi’s maintained NII ex-Markets guide looked better by comparison, and JPM / GS / CIB-heavy models looked less exposed than WFC to pure margin pressure.

KEY ISSUES TO MONITOR

NII inflection
Why it matters: The $50B FY target requires sequential improvement after a weak Q1 run-rate.

NIM stabilization
Why it matters: Loan growth only matters for the stock if it converts into higher-quality spread income.

Expense run-rate
Why it matters: Q1 expenses annualize above guidance, so H2 discipline is needed to protect operating leverage.

BOTTOM LINE

Mixed but not broken quarter.
The franchise is growing, but the EPS beat was low quality and the NII / NIM signal moved the wrong way.
The next issue is whether Wells can turn loan growth into sequential NII improvement rather than simply growing the balance sheet at lower margins.

<<WFC_EARNINGS_END>>

ZeroHedge framing: Characterized as results that "rekindled the same fears as those unveiled three months ago" when Q4 soft guidance had previously sent the stock lower. Drew explicit parallel to the Q4 cycle — suggesting pattern recognition among short sellers. Zero Hedge
Layer 4 named professional social commentary deferred — no individual analyst social posts confirmed readable.

LAYER 5 — NARRATIVE CLUSTERS
Cluster 1: WBD termination fee distorts the optics
Theme: Reported EPS of $1.23 is headline-grabbing but not operational. The market stripped this immediately. The "real" earnings print is more modest, and Q2 faces the highest content amortization growth rate of the year.
Support: Layers 0, 2A, 3 Signal 1
Confidence: High
Cluster 2: Setup problem, not fundamental problem
Theme: Stock had run 40–50% on WBD-exit relief. Expectations for Q2 guide raise were baked in. The market priced a "prove it" moment; guidance didn't deliver the raise. Jefferies explicitly frames this as setup, not deterioration.
Support: Layers 2A, 3 Signal 5, Layer 4
Confidence: High
Cluster 3: Hastings exit as symbolic overhang
Theme: Last co-founder governance anchor departing. Operationally immaterial (he left CEO role in 2023). Narratively it adds to a sense of transition at a moment when the company is also post-deal and setting a new chapter.
Support: Layers 2A, 3 Signal 2
Confidence: Medium
Cluster 4: Subscriber opacity creates structural market vulnerability
Theme: No quarterly sub count + Q2 content amortization peak + US pricing yield uncertainty = market cannot independently validate the membership and monetization thesis for another quarter.
Support: Layers 1, 3 Signal 4, 2B
Confidence: High
Cluster 5: Ad business and pricing as durable multi-year growth engines
Theme: Advertising on track to double to $3B. Price increases accepted without visible churn. BofA and broader analyst community views pricing power as structural strength. This is the bull case that survives the sell-off.
Support: Layers 1, 2A (BofA), 3 Signal 5 (framing)
Confidence: Medium-High

LAYER 6 — NARRATIVE VS DATA DIVERGENCE
Data signal: Revenue +16%, operating margin 32.3% (+60bps YoY), operating income +18%, advertising on track, global engagement metric at all-time high. Full-year guidance maintained. Organic fundamentals are solid.
Narrative signal: Market sold the stock 9–10% after hours. The guide miss on Q2 (revenue and EPS both below Street) combined with Hastings exit and no upward FY revision was read as failure to justify the 40–50% pre-print rally. ZeroHedge explicitly pattern-matched to Q4's similar dynamic.
Divergence: Strong. The fundamental print was strong. The market reaction was to the gap between elevated expectations and a maintained (not raised) guide in the context of maximum H1 content amortization pressure. The stock move reflects positioning and setup as much as the operating results. The organic business is not impaired — but the market needed a raise, got a hold, and sold.
Market relevance: The key question for the next quarter is whether Q2's elevated content amortization resolves into an H2 margin acceleration as management projects. If it does, the sell-off was a buying opportunity in a structurally strong business. If margins miss again in Q2, the narrative of a "peak Netflix" phase becomes harder to dismiss. The Hastings departure is a secondary but real symbolic risk in the near term.
State transition: False dawn — The post-WBD-exit rally was pricing a clean organic growth reaffirmation; the maintained guide without a raise, elevated content costs in Q2, and the founder departure triggered an unwind of that expectation despite a fundamentally solid operational quarter.

OFFICIAL EARNINGS DETAIL

Revenue / Sales:
Total revenue was $5.409B, up 13% YoY and 4% QoQ. Total fee revenue was $3.768B, up 11% YoY. Net interest income was $1.370B, up 18% YoY.

Consensus:
Quiver consensus was $1.99 EPS and $5.335B revenue. Zacks consensus referenced $1.94 EPS and $5.15B revenue. The company beat both top-line and EPS expectations across the available consensus markers.

EPS / Earnings:
Diluted EPS was $2.24, up 42% YoY. Adjusted diluted EPS was $2.25. Net income applicable to common shareholders was $1.562B, up 36% YoY.

Profitability / Margins:
Pre-tax operating margin was 37%, up from 32% in Q1 2025. ROTCE was 29.3%, up from 24.2% in Q1 2025. Noninterest expense was $3.400B, up 5% YoY, well below revenue growth.

Key KPI:
AUC/A was $59.4T, up 12% YoY. AUM was $2.1T, up 6% YoY. Securities Services revenue rose 17% YoY and Market and Wealth Services revenue rose 11% YoY.

Guidance headline:
No formal EPS guidance was provided in the release. The forward debate is whether fee revenue and NII strength can sustain once Q1 volatility and activity levels normalize.

Capital allocation:
BNY returned $1.4B to common shareholders, including $376M of dividends and $983M of repurchases. The Board authorized a new $10B common share repurchase program.

Other relevant official details:
Average deposits rose 13% YoY to $318.4B and average loans rose 16% YoY to $81.1B. CET1 was 11.0%, Tier 1 leverage was 6.0%, average LCR was 111% and average NSFR was 131%.

SEGMENT / BUSINESS BREAKDOWN

SEGMENT TABLE
